Whitney anukramaс╣З─л

[S─Бvitr─л S┼лry─Б.тАФ─Бtmad─Бivatam (1-5. somam ast─Бut; 6-тМК?тМЛ. svaviv─Бham; 23. som─Бrk─Бu; 24. candramasam;тАФ25тМК?тМЛ-тМК?тМЛ. nс╣Ыс╣З─Бс╣Б viv─Бhamantr─Б┼Ыiс╣гah; 25, 27. vadh┼лv─Бsaс╕еsaс╣Бspar┼Ыamocany─Бu). тМКAs to the foregoing, see above, p. 739.тМЛ ─Бnuс╣гс╣нubham: 14. vir─Бс╣н prast─Бrapan╠Дkti; 15. ─Бst─Бrapan╠Дkti; 19, 20, 23, 24, 31-33, 37, 39, 40, 45, 47, 49, 50, 53, 56, 57, [58, 59, 61]. triс╣гс╣нubh (23, 31, 45. bс╣Ыhat─лgarbh─Б); 21, 46, 54, 64. jagati (54, 64. bhurik triс╣гс╣нubh); 29, 55. purast─Бdbс╣Ыhat─л; 34. prast─Бrapan╠Дkti; 38. purobс╣Ыhat─л 3-p. paroс╣гс╣Зih; [48. pathy─Бpan╠Дkti;] 60. par─Бnuс╣гс╣нubh.]

Whitney

Comment

The hymn (except vss. 4, 62, which are wanting altogether, and 41, 42, which occur in other books) is found also in P─Бipp. xviii., with petty differences of order, noted under the verses. A large part of the anuv─Бka or hymn corresponds to the wedding hymn (x. 85) in the Rig-Veda. The V─Бit. does not treat the marriage ceremony, and only four or five of the verses of the book are quoted by it; but a large part of them are used in the sections (75-79) of the K─Бu┼Ы. which deal with the subject.

Translations

Translated: in so far as it corresponds to RV. verses, by the RV. translators; further, the parts that are peculiar to our text, by Ludwig, p. 470; and, as AV. hymn, all of it, by Weber, Ind. Stud. v. 195-204 (see 178 ff.); Griffith, ii. 159.тАФ-A large part of the wedding-hymn is given in my Sanskrit Reader, pages 89-90: the notes thereon (at pages 389-390) may be consulted, and also the notes at pages 398-401.

Griffith

On the Bridal of Surya, marriage ceremonies in general

Translation
  1. By truth is the earth established (ut-stabh); by the sun is the sky
    established; by righteousness the ─Аdityas stand; Soma is set (┼Ыrit├б)
    upon the sky.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 85. 1, without variant. The pada-text also reads
├║ttabhit─Б, by Pr─Бt. iv. 62, the s being omitted by ii. 18. K─Бu┼Ы.
directs vss. 1 and 23 to be used in preparing the sacrificial fire, at
the beginning of the chapter on the marriage-rites (75. 6: according to
the comm., vss. 1-16 are meant, and 23-24); and again, near the end of
the chapter (79. 16), the whole book is directed to be so used. тМКPpp.
has satvena for satyena at the beginning.тМЛ тМКCf. MP. i. 6. 1, and
Wint., p. 66.тМЛ

Griffith

Truth is the base that bears the earth; by Surya are the heavens upheld. By Law the Adityas stand secure, and Soma holds his place in heaven.

Whitney
Translation
  1. One thinks himself to have drunk Soma when they crush up an herb;
    what Soma the priests (brahm├бn) know, of that no earthly man partakes.
Notes

RV. (x. 85. 3) reads at the end k├б┼Ы can├б for p─Б╠Бrthivas. In b,
Bs.P.M.W.T. read -piс╣гanti, D. -p─лс╣гanti; Ppp. has -pi┼Ыanti. The
prat─лka is quoted in GB. i. 2.9 тМКprinted 8тМЛ.

Griffith

One thinks, when men have brayed the plant, that he hath drunk the Soma’s juice. Of him whom Brahmans truly know as Soma never mortal eats.

Whitney
Translation
  1. When, O Soma, they drink thee тМКupтМЛ, then thou fillest thyself up
    again; V─Бyu is Soma’s defender; the month is norm (─Б╠Бkс╣Ыti) of the years
    (s├бm─Б).
Notes

RV. (x. 85. 5) reads deva for soma in a. The verse (as noted
above) is wanting in Ppp.

Griffith

When they begin to drink thee, then, O God, thou swellest out again. Vayu in Soma’s sentinel. The month is that which shapes the years.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Guarded by covering-arrangements, defended by watchmen (??
    b├бrhata), O Soma, thou standest hearing the pressing-stones; no
    earthly one partakes of thee.
Notes

Is RV. X. 85. 4, without variant. All this talk about the moon as
identical with Soma at the beginning of the S┼лry─Б-hymn seems very
meaningless unless S┼лry─Б is really the moon, who every month “goes to”
her spouse the sun.

Griffith

Soma, preserved by covering rules, guarded by hymns in Brihati, Thou standest listening to the stones; none tastes of thee who dwells on earth.

Translation
  1. Intention (c├нtti) was the pillow, sight was the ointment, heaven
    [and] earth were the coffer (k├│┼Ыa), when S┼лry─Б went to her husband.
Notes

Is RV. x. 85. 7, without variant.

Griffith

Thought was her coverlet, the power of sight was unguent for her eyes: Her treasure-chest was earth and heaven, when Surya went unto her lord.

Translation
  1. The bridal (vahat├║) of S┼лry─Б, which Savitar sent off (ava-sс╣Ыj),
    has gone forth; in the Magh─Бs are slain the kine; in the Phalgun─лs is
    the wedding.
Notes

RV. (x. 85. 13) reads in c agh─Б╠Бsu* тМКPpp. has the sameтМЛ, and
hanyante without the antithetical accent which all our mss. give, and
which our text ought to read, and, for d, ├бrjunyoс╕е p├бry uhyate.
The Magh─Б stars are what we call the Sickle, in the neck of Leo; the
Phalgun─л stars are the rectangle ╬▓, ╬╕, ╬┤ 93 Leonis; arjun─л = phalgun─л;
the moon is in the latter either one or two days after it is in the
former.тАа From such utterly indefinite data the attempt to extract a date
is wasted labor. ‘Is the wedding’: vy ├╣hyate is the verb corresponding
to viv─Бha ‘wedding,’ lit. ‘driving away’; Ppp. reads instead vi
havyate. The second half-verse is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 75. 5, in the general
definition of the time for wedding. тМКWith reference to this
much-discussed verse, see: Weber, in Abh. der Berliner Ak. for 1861
(Nakс╣гatra-essay), p. 364, and in Sb. for 1894, p. 804; Jacobi,
Festgruss an Roth, p. 69; Wint., p. 32.тМЛ

*тМКWeber discusses the readings agh─Б╠Бsu and magh─Б╠Бsu, and deems the
RV. reading to be in this case the secondary one: Sb. 1894, p. 807.тМЛ
тАатМКConcerning these asterisms (no’s 10, and 11, 12) see Whitney, JAOS.
vi. 332-4, or Oriental and Linguistic Studies, ii. 352-3. It is not
impertinent to note that the regents of the Phalgun─лs are Bhaga and
Aryaman, and that those of the Magh─Бs are the Manes. For the latter, cf.
TB. iii. 1. 4тБ╕: s├│ тАШtra juhoti: pitс╣Ы╠Бbhyaс╕е sv─Б╠Бh─Б, magh─Б╠Бbhyaс╕е sv─Б╠Бh─Б,
тАЩnagh─Б╠Бbhyaс╕е sv─Б╠Бh─Б, gad─Б╠Бbhyaс╕е sv─Б╠Бh─Б, тАЩrundhat─л╠Бbhyaс╕е sv─Б╠Бhe, тАЩti; but
better TS. iv. 4. 10.тМЛ

Griffith

The bridal pomp of Surya, which Savitar started, moved along. In Magha days are oxen slain, in Phalgunis they wed the bride.

Whitney
Translation
  1. When, O A┼Ыvins, ye went asking, with your three-wheeled [chariot],
    to S┼лry─Б’s bridal, where was one wheel of yours? where stood ye for
    pointing out?
Notes

The verse corresponds, without variant, to RV. x. 85. 14 a, b and 15
c, d. The sense of the questions is wholly obscure.

Griffith

When on your three-wheeled chariot, O ye Asvins, ye came as suitors unto Surya’s bridal, Where was one chariot-wheel of yours? Where stood ye for the sire’s command?

Whitney
Translation
  1. When ye went, O lords of beauty, unto the wooing of S┼лry─Б, all the
    gods assented to that [deed] of yours; P┼лshan as son chose a father.
Notes

This verse, again, corresponds to parts of two in the RV., namely x. 85.
15 a, b and 14 c, d; the only variant is that RV. reads
pit├бr─Бu for -ram in d, and Ppp. pitar─Б тАЩvс╣Ы-, which doubtless
means the same. Metrically the verse is as much vir─Бj as vs. 14.

Griffith

Twin Lords of Lustre, at the time when ye to Surya’s wooing came, Then all the Gods agreed to your proposal Pushan as son elected you as father.

Two wheels of thine the Brahmans know, Surya! according to their times. That which is hidden only those who know the highest truths have learned.

Translation
  1. We make offering to Aryaman of good connections, husband-finder;
    like a gourd from its bond, from here I release, not from yonder.

and MS. (i. 10. 4), except that they accent sugandh├нm in b; VS.

for d, it├│ mukс╣г─лya m─Б╠Б тАЩm├║taс╕е. Ppp. has at end mu├▒ca m─Б тАШmutaс╕е.

Translation
  1. I release [her] from here, not from yonder; I make her well-bound
    yonder, that she, O gracious Indra, may be rich in sons, well-portioned.

Griffith

Hence and not thence I send her free. I make her softly fettered there. That, bounteous Indra! she may live blest in her fortune and her sons.

тМКMP. i. 5. 16тМЛ. Ppp. puts the verse next after our vs. 16; тМКbut further
it makes our 19 c, d change place with our 58 c, d, reading,
however, тАШstu sahapatn─л vadh┼л for our astu sah├бsambhal─Бyai.

Griffith

Now from the noose of Varuna I free thee, where with the bless- ed Savitar hath bound thee. May bless be thine together with thy wooer in Order’s dwelling, in the world of virtue.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let Bhaga lead thee hence, grasping thy hand; let the A┼Ыvins carry
    thee forth by a chariot; go to the houses, that thou mayest be
    housewife; thou, having control, shalt speak unto the council.
Notes

RV. (x. 85. 26) begins with p┼лс╣г─Б╠Б instead of bh├бgas. In K─Бu┼Ы. (76.
10) the verse accompanies the leading of the bride out of her house.

Griffith

Let Bhaga take thy hand and hence conduct thee: let the two Asvins on their car transport thee. Go to the house to be the household’s mistress, and speak as lady to thy gathered people.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let what is dear succeed (sam-с╣Ыdh) here for thy progeny; watch
    thou over this house in order to housewife-ship; mingle thy self
    (tan┼л╠Б) with this husband; then shalt thou in advanced age speak to the
    council.
Notes

RV. (x. 85. 27) reads in a praj├бy─Б (as does also Ppp.), and in
c-d sс╣Ыjasv─Б╠Б тАЩdh─Б j├нvr─л vidd├бtham ─Б╠Б vad─Бthaс╕е. Our d is the same
with viii. 1. 6 d above, and our mss. here also read j├нrvis
(except Bs.I., j├нvis), which ought to have been adopted in our text.
The ─Аpastamba text (Winternitz, p. 74 тМКMP. i. 9. 4тМЛ) has j─лvr─л. The
verse, with several others, is quoted in K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 20 in connection with
the bride^s entering her new abode. The verse lacks two syllables of
being a full jagat─л. тМКVs. discussed by Bloomfield, JAOS. xix.┬▓ 14; cf.
Baunack, KZ. xxxv. 495, 499.тМЛ

Griffith

Happy be thou and prosper with thy children here: be vigilant to rule the household in this home. Closely unite thy body with this man thy lord. So shalt thou, full of years, address thy company.

Whitney
Translation
  1. These two move on one after the other by magic; two sporting young
    ones go about the ocean; the one looks abroad upon all beings; thou, the
    other, disposing the seasons art born new.
Notes
Griffith

Moving by magic power from east to westward, these children twain go sporting round the ocean. The one beholds all creatures: thou, the other, art born anew, duly arranging seasons.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Ever new art thou, being born; sign of the days, thou goest to the
    apex of the dawns; thou disposest to the gods their share as thou
    comest; thou extendest, O moon, a long life-time.
Notes

These two verses are repeated here from vii. 81. 1, 2; тМКsee the notes to
those verses: also the Anukr. extracts at p. 739, ┬╢4. which refer vs. 23
to sun and moon and vs. 24 to the moonтМЛ. Most of verse 23 we had also as
xiii. 2. 11. In order to make sure that the two right ones are
reproduced, all our mss. read here p┼лrv─Бpar├бс╣Б n├бvonavaс╕е (instead of,
as usual, p┼лrv─Бpar├бm ├нti dv├й). They are RV. x. 85. 18, 19, and are
found also in other texts, as to which and the various readings see the
notes to vii. 81. 1, 2. Ppp. has in 23 d (with RV.) j─Бyate punaс╕е,
and in 24 (also with RV.) bhavati, eti, and dadh─Бti (but
apparently tirase). In K─Бu┼Ы. 75. 6, vs. 23 (according to the comm.,
both 23 and 24) is used with vs. 1; in 79. 28, vs. 64 is allowed instead
of vs. 24, in case the latter is not known.

Griffith

Thou, born afresh, art new and new for ever; ensign of days, before the Dawns thou goest. Coming, thou orderest for Gods their portion. Thou lengthenest, Moon, the days of our existence.

Griffith

Give thou the wollen robe away: deal treasure to the Brahman- priests. This Witchery hath got her feet: the wife attendeth on her lord.

Whitney
Translation
  1. It becomes blue-red; [as] witchcraft, infection, it is driven away
    (?); her relations (j├▒─Бt├н) thrive; her husband is bound in bonds.
Notes

Is RV. X. 85. 28, without variant. Vy ├аjyate is translated as coming
from root aj instead of a├▒j, ‘is smeared.’ P─Бda a perhaps refers
to the bloody discoloration of the garment; d to its ill effects if
not duly expiated. The ─Аp.-text (Wint., p. 67 тМКMP. i. 6. 8тМЛ) has for a
n─лlalohit├й bhavataс╕е, as if the garments were two. RV. and AV.
pada-texts have ─Бsakt─лс╕е undivided.

Griffith

It turneth dusky-red: the witch who clingeth close is driven off. Well thrive the kinsmen of this bride: the husband is bound fast in bonds.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Harsh is that, sharp, barbed, poisoned; that is not to be eaten;
    what priest (brahm├бn) knows S┼лry─Б, he indeed deserves the bride’s
    [garment].
Notes

RV. (x. 85. 34) inserts another et├бt after k├бс╣нukam, and reads
vidy─Б╠Бt for v├йda in c. The omission of k├бс╣нukam (with, in RV.,
et├бt) would rectify the meter of a; as it stands, it is an
extremely poor “bс╣Ыhat─л” p─Бda. ├Бttave ’to be eaten’ is very strange
here. S┼лry─Б in c is generally understood to mean ’the S┼лry─Б-hymn.’

The following four verses are found in no other text.

Griffith

Pungent is this, bitter is this, filled as it were with arrow barbs, empoisoned and not fit for use. The Brahman who knows Surya well deserves the garment of the bride.

Translation
  1. That priest verily takes this garment, pleasant, well-omened, who
    goes over the expiation, by whom the wife takes no harm.
Notes

The pada-text reads pr─Б╠Бya┼Ыcittim, undivided; if we had -ttam,
y├йna would apply to it, instead of to brahm─Б╠Б. Ppp. reads, for a,
b: sa v─Бi taс╣Б syono harati brahma v─Бsas suman╠Дgalan.

Griffith

The Brahman takes away the robe as a fair thing that brings good luck. He knows the expiating rite whereby the wife is kept unharmed.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Do ye (two) bring together a successful (s├бmс╣Ыddha) portion,
    speaking right in right-speakings; O Brahmaс╣Зaspati, make the husband
    shine (ruc) for her; let the wooer (sambhal├б) speak this speech
    agreeably (c─Б╠Бru).
Notes

According to K─Бu┼Ы. 75. 8, 9, this verse is addressed to the wooer and
his companion, when they are sent out to win the bride; the second
half-verse to the priest (who is one of them?). ‘Make shine,’ doubtless
‘set in a favorable light’ The verse тМКscanned by the Anukr. as 11 + 9:
12 + 12 = 44тМЛ may best be read as 11 + 11: 12 + 12; тМКbut d has a bad
cadenceтМЛ. Ppp. reads mс╣Ыtyodyena at end of b, and с╣гumbhalo in
d.

Griffith

Prepare, ye twain, happy and prosperous fortune, speaking the truth in faithful utterances. Dear unto her, Brihaspati, make the husband, and pleasant be these words the wooer speaketh.

Whitney
Translation
  1. May ye be just here; may ye not go away; may ye, O kine, increase
    this man with progeny; going in beauty, ruddy, with soma-splendorтАФmay
    all the gods turn (kс╣Ы) your minds hither.
Notes

In K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 17 this verse (according to the commentators, this and the
next) seems to be directed to accompany the paying (in kine) the price
demanded for the bride; but surely that cannot have been its original
sense. The first p─Бda is identical with iii. 8. 4 a; c has a
redundant syllable. The pada-text writes ┼Ы├║bham: yat─лс╕е, but the
expression is, so far as accent is concerned, treated as if a compound:
compare 2. 52 below. No reason is discoverable for the accent of kr├бn
in d.

Griffith

Remain ye even here and go no farther: strengthen this man, ye Cows, with plenteous offspring. May Dawns that come for glory, bright with Soma, here may all Gods fix and enchant your spirits.

Whitney
Translation
  1. May ye, O kine, enter this man together with progeny; this man
    minisheth (m─л) not the share of the gods; for this man shall P┼лshan,
    and all the Maruts, for this man shall Dh─Бtar, Savitar quicken (s┼л)
    you.
Notes

Ppp. reads vi┼Ыadhvam at end of a. This verse indicates distinctly
that the preceding one is meant as a wish for prosperity in respect to
kine.

Griffith

Come, O ye Cows, with offspring dwell around him: he doth not stint the Gods’ alloted portion. To him, your friend, may Pushan, all the Maruts, to him may Dhatar, Savitar send vigour.

Translation
  1. Free from thorns, straight, let the roads be by which [our]
    comrades go a-wooing for us; together with Bhaga, together with
    AryamanтАФlet Dh─Бtar unite [us] with splendor.
Notes

goes on: s├бm aryam─Б╠Б s├бm bh├бgo no nin─лy─Бt etc. тМКcf. MP. i. 1. 2тМЛ; our
text is a foolish and inconsistent substitute. K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 3 gives the
verse, with 2. 11, as to be used when the bridal train starts off home;
in 75. 12 it тМКaccording to Da┼Ыa Kar., only the first half-verseтМЛ is made
to accompany the sending out of a guard for the bride. тМКCf. Wint., p.
40.тМЛ

Griffith

Straight in direction be the paths, and thornless, whereby our fellows travel to the wooing. With Bhaga and with Aryaman Dhatar endue the pair with strength!

Whitney
Translation
  1. With what [splendor] the backsides of the courtezan (mah─Бnagn─л╠Б),
    O A┼Ыvins, or with what the strong drink, with what the dice were flooded
    (abhi-sic), with that splendor favor ye this woman.
Notes

That is, apparently, give her all the attractions which these various
seductive things are known to possess. ‘Courtezan,’ lit. ‘great naked
woman,’ emending to -nagny─Б╠Бs: тМКbut all authorities, both SPP’s and
W’s, have -naghny─Б╠БsтМЛ. The verse has a distant likeness to one in PGS.
ii. 6. 12. The с╣г of aс╣гicyanta is by Pr─Бt. ii. 92, where this example
is quoted in the commentary. The redundant syllable in the first p─Бda
passes unheeded by the Anukr. For the use of the verse in K─Бu┼Ы. see the
note to the preceding verse. Ppp. puts the verse before our 35 as noted
above, and the ms. reads for a: yan m─Б nagn─Б jaghnam.

Griffith

With all the sheen that balmeth wine, or thigh of female para- mour, With all the sheen that balmeth dice, even with this adorn the dame.

Whitney
Translation
  1. He who shines (d─л) without fuel within the waters, whom the devout
    (v├нpra) praise at the sacrifices (adhvar├б)тАФO child of the waters,
    mayest thou give waters rich in honey, with which Indra increased, full
    of heroism.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 30. 4, which accents d─л╠Бdayat, and reads at the end
v─лry─Б╠Аya. Ppp. combines in a yo тАШnidhmo. K─Бu┼Ы. 75. 14 makes the
verse accompany the piercing (pra-vyadh) of a stick of wood (loga)
in the water.

Griffith

He who in water shines unfed with fuel, whom sages worship in their sacrifices. May he, the Waters’ Child, send us sweet waters those that en- hanced the power of mighty Indra.

Translation
  1. Now do I remove (apa-┼лh) the glistening seizer (gr─Бbh├б),
    body-spoiling; what sheen is excellent, that I draw up (ud-ac).
Notes

Ppp. reads in the first half-verse tan┼лd┼лс╣гim athi nud─Бmi. For its
second half it has ya┼Ы ┼Ыivo bhadro rocanas tena tv─Бm api nud─Бmi,
making a fair half-anuс╣гс╣нubh. According to K─Бu┼Ы. 75. 15, 16, the thing
(the pierced piece of wood) is removed with the first two p─Бdas; and
with the third water is drawn up (anv─лpam ‘in the direction of the
current’) and is then presented with vs. 39. The verse (9 + 8: 11 = 28)
is described by the Anukr. with mechanical correctness.

  1. Let the Brahmans take for her [water] for bathing; let them draw
    up (?) waters that slay not a hero; let her go about the fire of
    Aryaman, O P┼лshan; father-in-law and brother-in-law are looking on
    (prati-─лkс╣г).

kс╣гipr├бm pr├бt─л тАЭkс╣гant─Бс╣Б ┼Ыva┼Ыr├║vo dev├бr─Б┼Ы ca. Ppp. reads in a-b ─Б
тАЩsm─Бi harantu snapanaс╣Б brahmaс╣З─Б тАЩv─лr-; and in c, тАШgniс╣Б pary eti
kс╣гipraс╣Б. тМКThe kс╣гipram of Ppp. and MP. suggests thatтМЛ our p┼лс╣гan in

Griffith

Hither let Brahmans bring her bathing water; let them draw such as guards the lives of heroes. Aryaman’s fire let her encircle, Pushan! Fathers-in-law stand, with their sons, expectant.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Weal be to thee gold, and weal be waters; weal be the post
    (meth├н), weal the perforation (t├бrdman) of the yoke; weal be for
    thee the waters having a hundred cleansers (-pav├нtra); for weal, too,
    mingle thyself with thy husband.
Notes

Ppp. is much corrupted in this verse, but can be seen to read metis
for methis in b; in c it combines t─Б тАЭpaс╕е, and in d it
omits u. In K─Бu┼Ы. 76. 12, the verse is muttered (according to the
paddhati, it and the following verse) while the bride is bound to the
right yoke-pole and the left yoke-hole, and a piece of gold is fastened
to her forehead. Purification by the yoke-hole (apparently growing out
of the occurrence of the next verse in RV.) plays a part in various
versions of the marriage-rites; тМКcf. note to vs. 41тМЛ. ─Аpast. (Wint., p.
44 тМКMP. i. 1. 10тМЛ) has this same verse with unimportant variations
(medh─л in b, etc). тМКCf. Wint., p. 46.тМЛ The verse (11 + 12: 11 + 11
= 45) is slightly irregular тМКbut has triс╣гс╣нubh-cndences throughoutтМЛ.

Griffith

Blest be the gold to thee, and blest the water, blest the yoke’s opening, and blest the pillar. Blest he the waters with their hundred cleansings: blest be thy body’s union with thy husband.

Whitney
Translation
  1. In the hole of the chariot, in the hole of the cart, in the hole of
    the yoke, O thou of a hundred activities, having thrice purified Ap─Бl─Б,
    O Indra, thou didst make her sun-skinned.

Griffith

Cleansing Apala, Indra! thrice, thou gavest sunbright skin to her Drawn, Satakratu! through the hole of car, of wagon, and of yoke.

Translation
  1. Hoping for well-willing, offspring, good-fortune, wealth, becoming
    obedient (├бnuvrata) to thy husband, gird thyself in order to
    immortality.
Notes

This verse also is found in Ppp. away from the rest, in book xx., and
with much difference of text: thus, b-d, praco bahur atho balam:
indr─Бс╣Зy anuvrat─Б san nahye amс╣Ыt─Бya kam. In K─Бu┼Ы. 76. 7, the verse is
used, with 2. 70, when the bride is girded with a bond, a yoke-rope
(yoktra). The ─Аpast. version (Wint., p. 45 тМКMP. i. 2. 7тМЛ) has tan┼л╠Бm
for ray├нm in b, agn├йr for p├бtyur in c, and, for d,
s├бс╣Б nahye sukс╣Ыt─Б╠Бya k├бm. V─Бit. 2. 6, again, makes it accompany the
girding of the sacrificer’s wife at the sacrifice. тМКIn the Berlin ed.,
correct kam to k├бm.тМЛ

Griffith

Saying thy prayer for cheerfulness, children, prosperity, and wealth, Devoted to thy husband, gird thyself for immortality.

Whitney
Translation
  1. As the тМКmighty (? vс╣Ы╠Бс╣г─Б)тМЛ river (s├нndhu) won (? s┼л) the
    supremacy of the streams (nad─л╠Б), so be thou supreme (samr─Б╠Бj├▒─л),

82. Ppp. reads s┼лс╣гuve vс╣Ыk─Бt. By K─Бu┼Ы. 75. 27, the verse accompanies
the emergence of the bride from the bath (with vs. 35, above).

Griffith

As vigorous Sindhu won himself imperial lordship of the streams, So be imperial queen when thou hast come within thy husband’s home.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Be thou supreme among fathers-in-law, supreme also among
    brothers-in-law; be thou supreme over sister-in-law, supreme also over
    mother-in-law.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 85. 46, which, however, reads for a, s. ┼Ыv├б┼Ыure
bhava; for b, s. ┼Ыva┼Ыrv─Б╠Бm bhava; for c, n├бn─Бndari s. bhava;
for d, s. ├бdhi devс╣Ы╠Бс╣гu; and MB. (i. 2. 20) agrees throughout with
RV. (┼Ыva┼Ыry─Бm in b must be a blunder). тМКMP. i. 6. 6 follows RV.,
but with ┼Ыva┼Ыruv─Б╠Бm in b: cf. Wint, p. 66.тМЛ

Griffith

Over thy husband’s fathers and his brothers be imperial queen. Over thy husband’s sister and, his mother bear supreme control.

Whitney
Translation
  1. They (f.) who spun, wove, and who stretched [the web], what
    divine ones (f.) gave the ends about, let them wrap thee in order to old
    age; [as] one long-lived put about thee this garment.
Notes

Ppp. combines in a y─Б тАЩkс╣Ыntan. The verse is found also in PCS. (i.
4. 13), HGS. (i. 4. 2), MB. (i. 1. 5). All end a with y─Б atanvata;
in b, all insert ca after y─Бs; and PGS. reads tant┼лn abhito*
tatantha, and MB. devyo ant─Бn abhito tatantha; for c, they have
t─Бs tv─Б dev─лr (MB. devyo) jaras─Б (PGS. -se) saс╣Бvyayantv (PGS.
-yasva); in d, only HGS. has ─Бyuс╣гm─Бn. тМКCf. MP. ii. 2. 5, and
Wint., p. 47, and MGS. i. 10. 8 and p. 154.тМЛ The verse has an extra
syllable in a which the Anukr. does not notice. In K─Бu┼Ы. 76. 4, this
and vs. 53 accompany the putting of a hitherto unused garment upon the
bride. тМКThe same two vss. are referred to by the name paridh─Бpan─лye at
79. 13: so the schol.тМЛ *тМКThis sandhi is of course not to be laid at the
door of the accurate Stenzler: it is doubtless the true reading of PGS.,
and occurs (not only in MB., but also) in Bhavadeva’s Paddhati, as
Stenzler observes in his Transl., p. 12.тМЛ

тМКThe corruption of abhito тАШdadanta (so AV.) to abhito tatantha (PGS.
MB. Bhavadeva) is of peculiar text-critical interest, not merely because
it is a senseless and unintelligent perversion, but because it is
revealed as a corruption by the ignorant failure of the persons
responsible for it to change their sandhi in such a way (abhitas
tatantha) as to fit their blunder.тАФThis interest is heightened by the
fact that we can see the probable occasion of the perversion, to wit,
the occurrence in the preceding p─Бda of the words for ‘spun,’ ‘wove,’
‘stretched web’ (root tan). These technical terms of clothmaking lend
a semblance of appropriateness to the introduction of tant┼лn tan
‘stretch the warp’ in p─Бda b.тАФRoth had already booked tatantha
among the cases of exchange between sonants and surds at ZDMG. xlviii.
108.тМЛ

Griffith

They who have spun, and woven, and extended Goddesses who have drawn the ends together, May they invest thee for full long existence. Heiress of lengthen- ed life, endue this garment,

Translation
  1. They bewail the living one (m.); they lead away the sacrifice
    (adhvar├б); the men sent their thoughts after тМКroot dh─л…├бnuтМЛ a long
    reach (pr├бsiti); what is lovely (v─Бm├б) for the Fathers who came
    together here; joy to the husbands for embracing the wife.
Notes

This is a literal version of this extremely obscure verse. RV. (x. 40.
10) reads in a v├н mayante adhvar├й; in b, the equivalent
d─лdhiyus тМКso also Ppp.тМЛ; in c, the equivalent samerir├й; in
d, j├бnayas (for our jan├бye, which might better have been emended
in the edition to j├бnaye); тМКPpp. reads and combines janayaс╣гтМЛ. The
─Аpast. text (Wint., p. 42 тМКMP. i. 1. 6тМЛ) reads at the beginning j─лv─Бm.
The verse is used, with 2. 59, in K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 30, simply to accompany a
libation, at the very close of the marriage rites. In two S┼лtras (AGS.
тМКi. 8. 4тМЛ and ┼ЫGS. тМКi. 15. 2тМЛ) it is directed to be used when the bride,
on the journey to her new home, wails or cries; this is plainly only on
account of the word ‘bewail’ (rudanti) at the beginning. тМКCf. Lanman’s
Skt. Reader, p. 387; Winternitz, p. 42; and Bloomfield, who devotes 9
pages to the stanza in AJP. xxi. 411-9.тМЛ

Griffith

They mourn the living, they arrange the sacred rite: the men have set their thoughts upon a distant cast: They who have brought the Fathers this delightful gift, when wives allowed their lords the joy of their embrace.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I maintain for thee, in order to progeny, a pleasant, firm
    (dhruv├б) stone in the lap of the divine earth; stand thou on that, one
    to be exulted after, of excellent glory; let Savitar make for thee a
    long life-time.
Notes

Ppp. puts syonam after dhruvam in a, reads pс╣Ыthivy─Бm in b,
and tam ─Б roh─Б тАЩnumady─Б suv─лr─Б for c, and tv─Б for te in d
тМКi.e., it has tv─Бyus for ta ─БyusтМЛ. In K─Бu┼Ы. 76. 15, the first
half-verse accompanies the setting of a stone in a lump of dung, and in
76. 16 the second accompanies the stepping of the bride upon it: this
at the bride’s home; and the same is repeated (K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 17, 19) in the
new home of the pair after their arrival there. P─Бda a has 12
syllables, unnoticed by the Anukr.

Griffith

I place upon the lap of Earth the Goddess, a firm auspicious stone to bring thee children. Stand on it, thou, greeted with joy, resplendent: a long long life may Savitar vouchsafe thee.

рд╕реНрдпреЛреТрдирдореНред рдзреНрд░реБреТрд╡рдореНред рдкреНрд░реТрд╜рдЬрд╛рдпреИреСред рдзрд╛реТрд░реТрдпрд╛реТрдорд┐реТред рддреЗреТред рдЕрд╢реНрдорд╛реСрдирдореНред рджреЗреТрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГред рдкреГреТрдерд┐реТрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГреТред рдЙреТрдкрд╜рд╕реНрдереЗреСред рддрдореНред рдЖред рддрд┐реТрд╖реНрдареТред рдЕреТрдиреБреТрд╜рдорд╛рджреНрдпрд╛реСред рд╕реБреТрд╜рд╡рд░реНрдЪрд╛рдГреСред рджреАреТрд░реНрдШрдореНред рддреЗреТред рдЖрдпреБрдГреСред рд╕реТрд╡рд┐реТрддрд╛ред рдХреГреТрдгреЛреТрддреБреТред рез.рекренред

Whitney
Translation
  1. Wherewith Agni grasped the right hand of this earth, therewith grasp
    I thy hand; do not stagger in company with me, with both progeny and
    riches.
Notes

after 50тМЛ. The verse accompanies in K─Бu┼Ы. 76. 19 the seizing of the

the vs.; though, if the last p─Бda were omitted, it would fall under the
general definition of the hymn, as an anuс╣гс╣нubh. тМКAs to vss. 48-51, cf.

Griffith

As Agni in the olden time took the right hand of this our Earth. Even so I take and hold thy hand: be not disquieted, with me, with children and with store of wealth.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let god Savitar grasp thy hand; let king Soma make thee to have good
    offspring; let Agni, J─Бtavedas, make the spouse well-portioned,
    long-lived, for her husband.
Notes

Ppp. has this verse next after our vs. 47, by removing тМКas notedтМЛ 48 to
after 50. The Anukr. takes no notice of the deficiency of two syllables
in c.

Griffith

God Savitar shall take thy hand, and Soma the King shall make thee rich in goodly offspring, Let Agni, Lord Omniscient, make thee happy, till old old age a wife unto thy husband.

Griffith

I take thy hand in mine for happy fortune that thou mayst reach old age with me thy consort, Gods, Aryaman, Bhaga, Savitar, Purandhi, have given thee to be my household’s mistress.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Bhaga hath grasped thy hand; Savitar hath grasped thy hand; thou art
    [my] spouse by ordinance (dh├бrman), I thy house-lord.
Notes

Ppp. reads dh─Бt─Б for bhagas in a, inserts te before hastam
in b, and adds after b two p─Бdas: bhagas te h. a. and aryam─Б
te h. a., тМКthen finishing with our c, dтМЛ. One of the subsidiary
treatises (see note to K─Бu┼Ы. 76. 10) substitutes the verse for vs. 20
above (see note there).

Griffith

Bhaga and Savitar the God have clasped that hand of thine in theirs, By rule and law thou art my wife: the master of thy house am I.

a, both have dhruv─Бi тАЩdhi poс╣гye (RV. -с╣гy─Б) mayi. тМКSee also MP.
i. 8. 9: that also has praj─Б╠Бvat─л.тМЛ

    of Brihaspati, of the poets; therewith let Savitar and Bhaga envelop

Tvashtar, by order of the holy sages, hath laid on her Brihas- pati’s robe for glory, By means of this let Savitar and Bhaga surround this dame, like Surya, with her children.

Griffith

May Indra-Agni, Heaven-Earth, Matarisvan, may Mitra-Varuna, Bhaga, both the Asvins, Brihaspati, the host of Maruts, Brahma, and Soma magnify this dame with offspring.

has for a third time n─Бryaс╣Б.тМЛ In K─Бu┼Ы. 79. 14 the verse is made to

Griffith

It was Brihaspati who first arranged the hair on Surya’s head, And therefore, O ye Asvins, we adorn this woman for her lord.

Whitney
Translation
  1. This [is] that form in which the young woman (y├│с╣г─Б) dressed
    herself; I desire to know with [my] mind the wife (j─Бy├б) moving
    about; I will go after her with nine-fold (? n├бvagva) comrades: who,
    knowing, unloosened (vi-cс╣Ыt) these fetters?
Notes

This obscure verse gets no light from Ppp., the other texts, or the
s┼лtras. The pada-text reads in c ├бnu: artiс╣гye; doubtless it is
only a contraction for ├бnu vartiс╣гye.

Griffith

This lovely form the maiden wears in spirit I long to look on as my wife approaching, Her will I follow with my nine companions. Who is the sage that loosed the bonds that held her?

Whitney
Translation
  1. I loosen (vi-s─Б) in me the form of her; he verily shall know,
    seeing the nest of mind; I eat not stolenly; I was freed (ud-muc) by
    mind, myself untying (┼Ыrath) the fetters of Varuс╣Зa.
Notes

Ppp. reads at the end p─Б┼Ыam. This verse and doubtless the next (its
prat─лka, which is pra tv─Б mu├▒c─Бmi, would also designate vs. 19
above) are used, with vii. 78. 1, by V─Бit. 4. 11, to accompany the
ungirding of the sacrificer’s wife. Both are used also by K─Бu┼Ы. 76. 28
with the ungirding of the bride.

Griffith

I free her: he who sees, within my bosom, my heart’s nest knows how her fair form hath struck me. I taste no stolen food: myself untying Varuna’s nooses I am freed in spirit.

Whitney
Translation
  1. I release thee from Varuс╣Зa’s fetter, with which the very propitious
    Savitar bound thee; wide space (lok├б), an easy road here, do I make
    for thee, O bride (vadh┼л╠Б), with thy husband.
Notes

The first half-verse is identical with vs. 19 a, b, and corresponds
with RV. x. 85. 24 a, b (which reads at end su┼Ы├йvaс╕е). Ppp. reads
for a-b im─Бс╣Б vi с╣гy─Бmi varuс╣Зasya p─Б┼Ыaс╣Б tena tv─Б etc.; тМКcf. the TS.
version of our 19 aтМЛ. тМКAs noted under vs. 19, Ppp. makes our 58 c,
d change place with our 19 c, d, reading, however, s┼лgam itra
for our sug├бm ├бtra and sahapatn─л vadh┼лс╕е for our sah├бpatny─Бi
vadhu.тМЛ Vss. 58, 59, 61 appear to be overlooked by the Anukr.,
probably by a loss of something out of the text: this (11 + 11: 10 + 12
= 44) is an irregular triс╣гс╣нubh; тМКthe longer form p├бnth─Бnam would
relieve the difficulty: cf. vs. 34, where, as between the longer and
shorter equivalent forms, our text is most clearly at faultтМЛ.

Griffith

Now from the bond of Varuna I loose thee, wherein the blessed Savitar hath bound thee. O bride, I give thee here beside thy husband fair space and room and pleasant paths to travel.

Translation
  1. Raise ye [your weapons]; may ye smite away the demon; set this
    woman in what is well done; inspired Dh─Бtar found for her a husband; let
    king Bhaga go in front, foreknowing.

the Ppp. variant bh┼лmyaс╣Б for bh┼л╠Бmim, xiii. 2. 40, 41.тМЛ

Griffith

Lift up your weapons. Drive away the demons. Transport this woman to the world of virtue. Dilator, most wise, hath found for her a husband. Let him who knows, King Bhaga, go before her.

Translation
  1. Bhaga fashioned the four feet; Bhaga fashioned the four frame-pieces
    (? ├║с╣гyala); Tvashс╣нar adorned (pi┼Ы) the straps (? v├бrdhra) along in
    the middle; let her be to us of excellent omen.
Notes

K─Бu┼Ы. uses the verse not only as stated in the preceding note, but also
(76. 25), more properly, with 2. 31, when the bride mounts the couch
(talpa). Ppp. reads in a padas; in b, catv─Бry aс╣гpad─Бni; in
c, madhyato varadhr─Бс╣Б. тМКFor ├║с╣гyala, cf. note to vi. 139. 3.тМЛ

and especially the note to XV. 5. 7.тМЛ

Griffith

Bhaga hath formed the four legs of the litter, wrought the four pieces that compose the frame-work. Tvashtar hath decked the straps that go across it, May it be blest, and bring us happy fortune.

Whitney
Translation
  1. The well-flowered (sukiс╣Е┼Ыuk├б), all-formed bridal-car (vahat├║),
    golden-colored, well-rolling, well-wheeled, do thou mount, O S┼лry─Б, to
    the world of the immortal; make thou a bridal -car pleasant to husbands.
Notes

The verse is RV. x. 85. 20, which reads ┼Ыalmal├нm in a for
vahat├║m, and in d p├бtye for p├бtibhyas, and kс╣Ыс╣Зuс╣гva for kс╣Ыс╣Зu
tv├бm. MB. (i. 3. 11) also has ┼Ыalmalim, patye, and kс╣Ыс╣Зuс╣гva, but
further in b suvarс╣Зavarс╣Зaс╣Б sukс╣Ыtam, and in c n─Бbhim for
lokam. тМКCf. MP. i. 6. 4; MGS. i. 13. 6 and p. 157.тМЛ K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 1
combines it with 2. 30, as used when the bride is made to mount the
vehicle that takes her to her new home. Ppp. has in c sukс╣Ыtasya
loke. The verse is a good triс╣гс╣нubh.

Griffith

Mount this, all-hued. gold tinted, strong wheeled, fashioned of Kinsuka, this chariot lightly rolling, Bound for the world of life immortal, Surya! Made for thy lord a happy bride’s procession.

    Brihaspati; not husband-slaying, possessing sons, O IndraтАФbring [her]
    for us, O Savitar.

indr─Б╠Б тАШputraghn─лс╣Б lakс╣гmy├ас╣Б t─Б╠Бm asy─Бi savitaс╕е suva. The Anukr. does not

Griffith

To us, O Varuna, bring her, kind to brothers; bring her, Brihas- pati, gentle to the cattle. Bring her, O Indra, gentle to her husband: bring her to us, O Savitar, blest with children.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Injure ye not the maiden (kum─Бr─л╠Б), ye (two) pillars, on the
    god-made road; the door of the divine house we make pleasant, a road for
    the bride.
Notes

Or, ‘we make a pleasant road’ etc. In K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 20, the verses 2. 26; 1.
21, 63, 64, in this order, are used to accompany the bride’s stepping
forward into the house. тМКCf. Wint., p. 72, top.тМЛ

Griffith

Hurt not the girl, ye Pillars twain upon the path which Gods have made. The portal of the heavenly home we make the bride’s auspicious road.

Whitney
Translation
  1. Let the br├бhman be yoked after, the br├бhman before, the
    br├бhman at the end, in the middle, the br├бhman everywhere; going
    forward to an impenetrable stronghold of the gods, do thou (f.),
    propitious, pleasant, bear rule in thy husband’s world.
Notes

Besides the use of the verse in K─Бu┼Ы. 77. 20, as noticed just above, it
is quoted, with 2. 8, in 77. 2, when the bride sets out, with a Brahman
in front. In 79. 28, it is allowed to be substituted for vs. 23; and in
that case (? 79. 32) the ceremony is called br─Бhmya instead of
s─Бurya.

тМКHere ends the first anuv─Бka, with 1hymn (but see page 739, top) and
64 verses. The quoted Anukr. says ─Бdyaс╕е s─Бurya┼Ы catuс╕ес╣гaс╣гс╣нiс╕е (see p.
738).тМЛ

Griffith

Let prayer he offered up before and after, prayer in the middle, lastly, all around her. Reaching the Gods’ inviolable castle shine in thy lord’s world gentle and auspicious.
